## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of population (dP_dt) as a function of time (t) and current population size (P). This is a classic population dynamics problem where growth rate depends on population size through various ecological mechanisms such as density dependence, Allee effects, and environmental carrying capacity.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Malthusian/exponential growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P', 'scenario': 'Unlimited exponential growth, growth rate proportional to population'}
- {'name': 'Logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Theta-logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)', 'scenario': 'Generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence'}
- {'name': 'Gompertz growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate decreasing logarithmically as population approaches carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Population with strong Allee effect (minimum viable population threshold)'}
- {'name': 'Weak Allee effect', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P)', 'scenario': 'Reduced growth at low density but no critical threshold'}
- {'name': 'Von Bertalanffy-type growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Balance between anabolic (power-law) and catabolic (linear) processes'}
- {'name': 'Richards growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2', 'scenario': 'Flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth'}
- {'name': 'Power-law growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1', 'scenario': 'Allometric scaling of population growth rate'}
- {'name': 'Time-varying logistic growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * exp(c2 * t)', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth with exponentially changing intrinsic rate'}
- {'name': 'Beverton-Holt continuous rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Growth with recruitment saturation and constant mortality'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3', 'scenario': 'Higher-order density-dependent effects'}
- {'name': 'Time-modulated growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth with seasonal/periodic environmental forcing'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Quadratic dependence on P (P - P²) → classic logistic density dependence with carrying capacity
- Cubic polynomial in P → Allee effect or bistability in population dynamics
- Logarithmic dependence log(K/P) → Gompertz-type growth with multiplicative decline in per-capita rate
- Product of P with (1 - P/K) structure → self-limiting growth approaching equilibrium
- Negative quadratic term in P → density-dependent mortality or competition effects dominating at high population
- Fractional power P^c with 0<c<1 → sub-linear metabolic scaling in population growth
- Sinusoidal modulation with time → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on growth rate
- Ratio P/(1+cP) → saturating per-capita resource acquisition (contest competition)

**GT expression:**
`0.1404201690960543*(-1 + P/4.5321236760653205)*(1 - P/78.49071311458529)*P + 0.1404201690960543*P/t**4.5321236760653205`

Let me expand the first part:
`0.1404 * (-1 + P/4.532) * (1 - P/78.49) * P`

Let me expand `(-1 + P/4.532)(1 - P/78.49)`:
= `-1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P²/(4.532*78.49)`
= `-1 + P(1/78.49 + 1/4.532) - P²/(355.7)`

So GT = `0.1404 * P * [-1 + P(1/78.49 + 1/4.532) - P²/355.7] + 0.1404*P/t^4.532`

This simplifies to:
= `0.1404*P*(-1) + 0.1404*P²*(1/78.49 + 1/4.532) - 0.1404*P³/(355.7) + 0.1404*P*t^(-4.532)`

Wait, let me reconsider. The GT has the structure:
**GT = a*P³ + b*P² + c*P + d*P/t^e**

where a, b, c, d, e are specific constants. More precisely:
- A cubic polynomial in P (with terms P³, P², P)
- Plus a term P/t^4.532

So the GT has basis functions: **P³, P², P, P·t^(-4.532)**

Now let me check each candidate systematically. I need candidates that can produce exactly these four basis function terms.

Let me go through candidates looking for those that can express: `α·P³ + β·P² + γ·P + δ·P·t^(-κ)` where κ ≈ 4.532.
